## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard dependent variable in chemical kinetics ODEs. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are empirical/mechanistic rate laws dA_dt = f(A,t) capturing reaction order, reversibility, autocatalysis, deactivation, or time-varying forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or excess reactant)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decomposition / pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- nth-order decay (power-law rate): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general reaction order fitting)
- Second-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order)
- Autocatalytic growth/decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating formation with limiting capacity / logistic-like kinetics in concentration space)
- Reversible first-order to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (relaxation of A toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible with mass-action forward/backward surrogate: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (production at constant source with first-order loss; CSTR-like lumped model)
- Inhibition / crowding-limited rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A + 1) (rate slows at high A due to inhibition, viscosity, or limited sites)
- Autoinhibition / saturation of consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (c2 * A**c1 + 1) (high-A plateau in depletion rate; generalized rational form)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (catalyst activation/deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective first-order with decaying activity over time)
- Time-ramping kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 * t + 1) * A (linearly changing apparent rate constant, e.g., temperature/program or mixing ramp)
- Oscillatory forcing of rate (periodic driving): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 * sin(c2 * t) + 1) * A (periodic modulation from cycling conditions)
- Nonlinear mixed time–concentration dependence: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (combined reaction order with time-varying activity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: dA_dt proportional to A**n (power-law) indicates nth-order kinetics; log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) is approximately linear.
- Equilibrium approach: dA_dt proportional to (c - A) implies exponential relaxation toward a steady-state/equilibrium concentration.
- Source–sink balance: constant production term plus first-order loss (c0 - c1*A) yields a stable steady state A* = c0/(c1) and monotone approach.
- Autocatalysis signature: factors like A*(c - A) produce sigmoidal time courses in A (slow start, acceleration, then slowdown) even though the ODE is first-order in time.
- Inhibition or site limitation: rational factors 1/(1 + c*A) or 1/(1 + c*A**n) capture diminishing marginal rate at high A (e.g., diffusion limits, adsorption-limited steps, catalyst poisoning).
- Catalyst deactivation/aging: multiplicative exp(-c*t) on a base rate law represents loss of activity with time, causing progressively slower dynamics even at the same A.
- Process/program effects: explicit t factors (c*t + 1) indicate externally controlled changes (heating ramps, feed ramps, mixing transients) rather than intrinsic kinetics.
- Periodic operation: sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) modulation reflects cycling reactors or periodic forcing, leading to alternating acceleration/deceleration of A consumption/production.
- Finite-time depletion constraints: strong nonlinearities (e.g., A**n with n>1) can yield rapid late-stage drop as A decreases, distinguishing them from exponential (first-order) tails.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK26)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A*exp(-c3*_s*t) + c4*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidates evaluated: 61
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can match the Ground Truth (GT):

$$f(t,A) = -0.3324 \cdot A^2 - 0.3324 \cdot A \cdot e^{-0.0707t} + 0.1365 \cdot \sin(\sqrt{A})$$

The GT has three basis functions:
1. $A^2$ (polynomial)
2. $A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$ (exponential decay times A)
3. $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ (sinusoidal function of sqrt(A))

The key challenge is matching $\sin(\sqrt{A})$. This is a specific transcendental function that cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, logarithms, power functions, or rational functions of A.

Let me check which candidates contain $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ or something that could produce it.

Looking through all candidates:
- Most candidates use combinations of: $A^{3/2}$, $\sqrt{A}$, $A^2$, $A \cdot e^{ct}$, $\log(cA+1)/\sqrt{A}$, $A^c \cdot c/(A^c \cdot c + 1)$, rational functions $A/(A+c)$, $\sqrt{A}\log(cA+1)$, etc.
- **Candidate 18**: Contains $c6 \cdot \sin(c7 \cdot \log(A \cdot c8 + 1) + c9)$ — this is $\sin$ of $\log$, not $\sin(\sqrt{A})$. $\log(cA+1) \neq \sqrt{A}$, so NO MATCH.
- **Candidate 22**: Contains $c6 \cdot \sin(c7 \cdot \log(A \cdot c8 + 1) + c9)$ — same issue, NO MATCH.
- **Candidate 53**: Contains $c6 \cdot \sin(c7 \cdot \log(A \cdot c8 + 1) + c9)$ — same issue, NO MATCH.

None of the candidates contain $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ directly. The question is whether any combination of the offered basis functions can exactly equal $\sin(\sqrt{A})$.

$\sin(\sqrt{A})$ cannot be expressed as any finite combination of:
- Powers of A ($A^c$, $\sqrt{A}$, $A^{3/2}$, etc.)
- $\log(cA+1)$, $\log(cA+1)/\sqrt{A}$, $\sqrt{A}\log(cA+1)$
- Rational functions of A
- $\sin(\log(\cdot))$ (different from $\sin(\sqrt{\cdot})$)
- $\log(c \cdot e^{f(A)} + 1)$ (softplus-type functions)

These are all fundamentally different function classes. Since $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ has infinitely many zeros (at $A = (n\pi)^2$) while polynomials, power laws, and logarithmic functions don't oscillate, no combination of non-oscillatory functions can match it.

For candidates with $\sin(\log(\cdot))$: $\log(cA+1)$ grows monotonically and unboundedly, so $\sin(\log(cA+1))$ does oscillate, but its zeros occur at exponentially spaced points, while $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ has quadratically spaced zeros. These cannot be equal.

Since the $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ term has coefficient $0.1365 \neq 0$, it cannot be dropped, and no candidate provides a basis function that can represent it.

Let me verify: could any candidate set the $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ coefficient to 0? No — the GT constants are FIXED. The GT has a non-zero $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ term that must be matched.

For all 61 candidates: **[NO MATCH]** — none contain $\sin(\sqrt{A})$ or any function that could be algebraically equivalent to it.
